	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Balkans</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Geopolitical and cultural region of southeastern Europe</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Balkans</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte_Suedosteuropa_03_01.png" class="image" title="The Balkan region according to Prof R. J. Crampton"><img alt="The Balkan region according to Prof R. J. Crampton" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Karte_Suedosteuropa_03_01.png/260px-Karte_Suedosteuropa_03_01.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="167" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Karte_Suedosteuropa_03_01.png/390px-Karte_Suedosteuropa_03_01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Karte_Suedosteuropa_03_01.png/520px-Karte_Suedosteuropa_03_01.png 2x" data-file-width="596" data-file-height="383" /></a><div>The Balkan states according to <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a><br /><div class="legend-line"><span style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:middle; width:1.67em; height:0px; border-style:none; border-top:2px dotted #000; border-top:solid darkblue 8px;">&#160;</span>&#160;The Balkan Peninsula using the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>–<a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a>–<a href="/wiki/So%C4%8Da" title="Soča">Soča</a> border</div><span style="background-color:#ff7b4d; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Political communities that are often included in the Balkans.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef">Geography</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Location</th><td><a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeastern Europe</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Coordinates</th><td><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Balkans&amp;params=42_N_22_E_source:wikidata_type:isle"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">42°N</span> <span class="longitude">22°E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">42°N 22°E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">42; 22</span></span></span></a></span><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Balkans&amp;params=42_N_22_E_source:wikidata_type:isle"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">42°N</span> <span class="longitude">22°E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">42°N 22°E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">42; 22</span></span></span></a></span></span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Area</th><td>470,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (180,000&#160;sq&#160;mi)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Highest&#160;elevation</th><td>2,925&#160;m (9,596&#160;ft)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Highest&#160;point</th><td><a href="/wiki/Musala" title="Musala">Musala</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>)</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef">Administration</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div><b><a href="/wiki/Balkans#Definitions_and_boundaries" title="Balkans">See below</a></b></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef">Demographics</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Population</th><td>ca. 55 million</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Balkans</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ɔː/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">ɔː</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">BAWL</span>-kənz</i></a>, also known as the <b>Balkan Peninsula</b>, is a geographic area in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a> with various definitions and meanings,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> including geopolitical and historical.<sup id="cite_ref-Schaefer2008_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaefer2008-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The region takes its name from the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Mountains" title="Balkan Mountains">Balkan Mountains</a> that stretch throughout the whole of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbian</a>–<a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgarian</a> border to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coast. The Balkan Peninsula is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> on the northwest, the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a> on the southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> in the south and southeast, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> on the east and northeast. The northern border of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> is variously defined.<sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The highest point of the Balkans is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Musala" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Musala">Mount Musala</a>, 2,925 metres (9,596&#160;ft), in the <a href="/wiki/Rila" title="Rila">Rila</a> mountain range, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>.
</p><p>The concept of the Balkan peninsula was created by the German geographer <a href="/wiki/August_Zeune" title="August Zeune">August Zeune</a> in 1808,<sup id="cite_ref-Tomic2006_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tomic2006-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> who mistakenly considered the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Mountains" title="Balkan Mountains">Balkan Mountains</a> the dominant mountain system of Southeast Europe spanning from the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. The term of Balkan Peninsula was a synonym for European Turkey in the 19th century, the former provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in Southeast Europe. It had a geopolitical rather than a geographical definition, further promoted during the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a> in the early 20th century. The definition of the Balkan peninsula's natural borders do not coincide with the technical definition of a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> and hence modern geographers reject the idea of a Balkan peninsula, while scholars usually discuss the Balkans as a region. The term has acquired a stigmatized and pejorative meaning related to the process of <a href="/wiki/Balkanization" title="Balkanization">Balkanization</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BideleuxJeffries2007_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BideleuxJeffries2007-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and hence the preferred alternative term used for the region is <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h3>
<p>The word <i>Balkan</i> comes from <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a> <i><i lang="tr" title="Turkish language text">balkan</i></i> 'chain of wooded mountains';<sup id="cite_ref-Balkan._8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balkan.-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> related words are also found in other Turkic languages.<sup id="cite_ref-oed_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oed-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The origin of the Turkic word is obscure; it may be related to <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> <i>bālk</i> 'mud', and the Turkish suffix <i>an</i> 'swampy forest'<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> or Persian <i>balā-khāna</i> 'big high house'.<sup id="cite_ref-Todorova_1997_27_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Todorova_1997_27-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_names_and_meaning">Historical names and meaning</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity_and_the_early_Middle_Ages">Classical antiquity and the early Middle Ages</span></h4>
<p>From <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the Balkan Mountains were called by the local <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> name "<a href="/wiki/Haemus" title="Haemus">Haemus</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> According to Greek mythology, the <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thracian</a> king <a href="/wiki/Haemus" title="Haemus">Haemus</a> was turned into a mountain by <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a> as a punishment and the mountain has remained with his name. A reverse name scheme has also been suggested. D. Dechev considers that Haemus (Αἷμος) is derived from a <a href="/wiki/Thracian_language" title="Thracian language">Thracian</a> word <i>*saimon</i>, 'mountain ridge'.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A third possibility is that "Haemus" (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Αἵμος</span>) derives from the Greek word "haima" (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">αἷμα</span>) meaning 'blood'. The myth relates to a fight between <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a> and the monster/titan <a href="/wiki/Typhon" title="Typhon">Typhon</a>. Zeus injured Typhon with a thunder bolt and Typhon's blood fell on the mountains, from which they got their name.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_Middle_Ages_and_Ottoman_period">Late Middle Ages and Ottoman period</span></h4>
<p>The earliest mention of the name appears in an early 14th-century Arab map, in which the <a href="/wiki/Haemus_Mons" title="Haemus Mons">Haemus mountains</a> are referred to as <i>Balkan</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dobrev_1989_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dobrev_1989-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The first attested time the name "Balkan" was used in the West for the mountain range in <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> was in a letter sent in 1490 to Pope <a href="/wiki/Innocent_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Innocent VIII">Innocent VIII</a> by Buonaccorsi Callimaco, an Italian humanist, writer and diplomat.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ottomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottomans">Ottomans</a> first mention it in a document dated from 1565.<sup id="cite_ref-Todorova_1997_27_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Todorova_1997_27-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> There has been no other documented usage of the word to refer to the region before that, although other Turkic tribes had already settled in or were passing through the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Todorova_1997_27_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Todorova_1997_27-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> There is also a claim about an earlier <a href="/wiki/Bulgar_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgar languages">Bulgar</a> Turkic origin of the word popular in Bulgaria, however it is only an unscholarly assertion.<sup id="cite_ref-Todorova_1997_27_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Todorova_1997_27-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The word was used by the Ottomans in <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a> in its general meaning of mountain, as in <i>Kod̲j̲a-Balkan</i>, <i>Čatal-Balkan</i>, and <i>Ungurus-Balkani̊</i>, but especially it was applied to the Haemus mountain.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The name is still preserved in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Daglary" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Daglary">Balkan Daglary</a> (Balkan Mountains)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Province">Balkan Province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>. English traveler <a href="/wiki/John_Morritt" class="mw-redirect" title="John Morritt">John Morritt</a> introduced this term into the English literature at the end of the 18th-century, and other authors started applying the name to the wider area between the Adriatic and the Black Sea. The concept of the "Balkans" was created by the German geographer <a href="/wiki/August_Zeune" title="August Zeune">August Zeune</a> in 1808,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> who mistakenly considered it as the dominant central mountain system of Southeast Europe spanning from the Adriatic Sea to the Black Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> During the 1820s, "Balkan became the preferred although not yet exclusive term alongside Haemus among British travelers... Among Russian travelers not so burdened by classical toponymy, Balkan was the preferred term".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_of_meaning_in_19th_and_20th_century">Evolution of meaning in 19th and 20th century</span></h3>
<p>The term was not commonly used in geographical literature until the mid-19th century because already then scientists like <a href="/wiki/Carl_Ritter" title="Carl Ritter">Carl Ritter</a> warned that only the part South of the Balkan Mountains can be considered as a peninsula and considered it to be renamed as "Greek peninsula". Other prominent geographers who didn't agree with Zeune were <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Wagner_(geographer)" title="Hermann Wagner (geographer)">Hermann Wagner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theobald_Fischer" title="Theobald Fischer">Theobald Fischer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marion_Newbigin" title="Marion Newbigin">Marion Newbigin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_Penck" title="Albrecht Penck">Albrecht Penck</a>, while Austrian diplomat <a href="/wiki/Johann_Georg_von_Hahn" title="Johann Georg von Hahn">Johann Georg von Hahn</a> in 1869 for the same territory used the term <i>Südostereuropäische Halbinsel</i> ("Southeasterneuropean peninsula"). Another reason it was not commonly accepted as the definition of then <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">European Turkey</a> had a similar land extent. However, after the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> (1878) there was a political need for a new term and gradually the Balkans was revitalized, but in the maps the northern border was in Serbia and Montenegro without Greece (it only depicted the Ottoman occupied parts of Europe), while Yugoslavian maps also included Croatia and Bosnia. The term Balkan Peninsula was a synonym for European Turkey, the political borders of former Ottoman Empire provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VezenkovIWM06_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VezenkovIWM06-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The usage of the term changed in the very end of the 19th and beginning of the 20th century when was embraced by Serbian geographers, most prominently by <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Cviji%C4%87" title="Jovan Cvijić">Jovan Cvijić</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It was done with political reasoning as affirmation for <a href="/wiki/Serbian_nationalism" title="Serbian nationalism">Serbian nationalism</a> on the whole territory of the <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a>, and also included anthropological and ethnological studies of the South Slavs through which were claimed various nationalistic and racistic theories.<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Through such policies and Yugoslavian maps the term was elevated to the modern status of a geographical region.<sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The term acquired political nationalistic connotations far from its initial geographic meaning,<sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> arising from political changes from the late 19th century to the creation of post–<a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> (initially the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbs,_Croats_and_Slovenes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes</a> in 1918).<sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dissolution of Yugoslavia">dissolution of Yugoslavia</a> beginning in June 1991, the term "Balkans" acquired a negative political meaning, especially in Croatia and Slovenia, as well in worldwide casual usage for war conflicts and fragmentation of a territory (see <a href="/wiki/Balkanization" title="Balkanization">Balkanization</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Europe">Southeast Europe</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a></div>
<p>In part due to the historical and political connotations of the term "Balkans",<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> especially since the military conflicts of the 1990s in <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> in the western half of the region, the term "<a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>" is becoming increasingly popular.<sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> initiative of 1999 is called the <i><a href="/wiki/Stability_Pact_for_South_Eastern_Europe" title="Stability Pact for South Eastern Europe">Stability Pact for South Eastern Europe</a></i>, and the online newspaper <i>Balkan Times</i> renamed itself <i><a href="/wiki/Southeast_European_Times" title="Southeast European Times">Southeast European Times</a></i> in 2003.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span></h3>
<p>In other languages of the region, the region is known as:
</p>
<ul><li>Slavic languages:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Балкански полуостров</span>, transliterated: <i><i lang="mk" title="Macedonian language text">Balkanski poluostrov</i></i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Балканско полуострво; Balkansko poluostrvo</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>: <i lang="bs">Balkansko poluostrvo; Балканско полуострво; Balkanski poluotok</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>: <i lang="hr">Balkanski poluotok</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene</a>: <i lang="sl">Balkanski polotok</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Romance languages:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i lang="ro">Peninsula Balcanică</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Turkic Languages:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Balkan Yarımadası</i> or <i>Balkanlar</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Other languages:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Gadishulli Ballkanik</i> and <i><i lang="sq" title="Albanian language text">Siujdhesa e Ballkanit</i></i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Βαλκανική χερσόνησος</span>, transliterated: <i><i lang="el" title="Greek language text">Valkaniki chersonisos</i></i></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions_and_boundaries">Definitions and boundaries</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Balkan_Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkan_topo_en.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Balkan_topo_en.jpg/220px-Balkan_topo_en.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Balkan_topo_en.jpg/330px-Balkan_topo_en.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Balkan_topo_en.jpg/440px-Balkan_topo_en.jpg 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="767" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkan_topo_en.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Balkan Peninsula, as defined by the <a href="/wiki/So%C4%8Da" title="Soča">Soča</a>–<a href="/wiki/Vipava_(river)" title="Vipava (river)">Vipava</a>–<a href="/wiki/Krka_River_(Slovenia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Krka River (Slovenia)">Krka</a>–<a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a>–<a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> border.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg/220px-Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg/330px-Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg/440px-Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="530" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkan_peninsula_line.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Peninsula's most extensive definition, bordered by water on three sides and connected with a line on the fourth</div></div></div>
<p>The Balkan Peninsula is bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Ionian sea">Ionian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aegean_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Aegean sea">Aegean</a> seas) and the <a href="/wiki/Marmara_Sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Marmara Sea">Marmara Sea</a> to the south and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> to the east. Its northern boundary is often given as the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kupa" title="Kupa">Kupa</a> Rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJelavich1983a1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJelavich1983a1-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2018)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Balkan Peninsula has a combined area of about 470,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (181,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) (slightly smaller than <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>). It is more or less identical to the region known as <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1920 until <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Italy included <a href="/wiki/Istria" title="Istria">Istria</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatian</a> areas (like <i>Zara</i>, today's <a href="/wiki/Zadar" title="Zadar">Zadar</a>) that are within the general definition of the Balkan peninsula. The current territory of Italy includes only the small area around <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> inside the Balkan Peninsula. However, the regions of Trieste and Istria are not usually considered part of the Balkans by Italian geographers, due to their definition of the Balkans that limits its western border to the Kupa River.<sup id="cite_ref-Agostini,_2004,_p.78_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agostini,_2004,_p.78-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Share of total area in brackets<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> within the Balkan Peninsula by country, by the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>-<a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> definition, with <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> occupying almost the half of the territory of the Balkan Peninsula, with around 23% of the total area each:
</p><p>Entirely within the Balkan peninsula:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/21px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png" decoding="async" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/32px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/42px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="700" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>: 28,749&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (100% of total land)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>: 51,180&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (100%)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>: 110,993.6<sup id="cite_ref-Penin_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penin-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>/ according to other sources 111,002&#160;km<sup>2</sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>(100%)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/21px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/32px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/42px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_status"><a href="#endnote_status">[a]</a></sup>: 10,908&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (100%)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/23px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/35px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/46px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="320" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>: 13,810&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (100%)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg/23px-Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg/35px-Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg/46px-Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1680" data-file-height="840" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>: 25,710&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (100%)</li></ul>
<p>Mostly or partially within the Balkan peninsula:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Croatia" title="Administrative divisions of Croatia">southern mainland</a>): 24,013&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (46%)<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pavić_Radovan_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pavić_Radovan-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>
