<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Balkans">Balkans</span></h3>
<p>The term "the Balkans" is used more generally for the region; it includes states in the region, which may extend beyond the peninsula, and is not defined by the geography of the peninsula itself.
</p><p>Historians state the Balkans comprise <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_status"><a href="#endnote_status">[a]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Its total area is usually given as 666,700&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (257,400&#160;sq&#160;mi) and the population as 59,297,000 (est. 2002).<sup id="cite_ref-EB_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Italy, although having a small part of its territory in the Balkan peninsula, is not included in the term "the Balkans".
</p><p>The term <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a> is also used for the region, with various definitions. Individual Balkan states can also be considered part of other regions, including <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>. Turkey, often including its European territory, is also included in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western</a> or <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Southwestern Asia">Southwestern Asia</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Balkans">Western Balkans</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2015_Western_Balkans_Summit,_Vienna" title="2015 Western Balkans Summit, Vienna">2015 Western Balkans Summit, Vienna</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Western_Balkans.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Western_Balkans.PNG/220px-Western_Balkans.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Western_Balkans.PNG/330px-Western_Balkans.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Western_Balkans.PNG/440px-Western_Balkans.PNG 2x" data-file-width="606" data-file-height="570" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Western_Balkans.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Western Balkan countries – <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. The partially recognized <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> is also demarcated. Croatia (yellow) joined the EU in 2013.</div></div></div>
<p><i>Western Balkans</i> is a political neologism coined to refer to Albania and the territory of the former <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, except <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, since the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> The region of the <i>Western Balkan</i>, a coinage exclusively used in Pan-European parlance, roughly corresponds to the <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric Alps</a> territory.
</p><p>The institutions of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> have generally used the term "Western Balkans" to mean the Balkan area that includes countries that are not members of the European Union, while others refer to the geographical aspects.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup>
Each of these countries aims to be part of the <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">future enlargement of the European Union</a> and reach democracy and transmission scores but, until then, they will be strongly connected with the pre-EU waiting program <a href="/wiki/CEFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="CEFTA">CEFTA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Croatia, considered part of the Western Balkans, joined the EU in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_the_geographical_definition">Criticism of the geographical definition</span></h2>
<p>The term is criticized for having a geopolitical, rather than a geographical meaning and definition, as a multiethnic and political area in the southeastern part of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The geographical term of a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> defines that the water border must be longer than land, with the land side being the shortest in the triangle, but that is not the case with the Balkan Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Both Eastern and Western water cathetus from <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Matapan" title="Cape Matapan">Cape Matapan</a> (ca. 1230–1350&#160;km) and from <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> to Cape Matapan (ca. 1270–1285&#160;km) are shorter than land cathetus from Trieste to Odessa (ca. 1330–1365&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The land has a too wide line connected to the continent to be technically proclaimed as a peninsula - <a href="/wiki/Szczecin" title="Szczecin">Szczecin</a> (920&#160;km) and <a href="/wiki/Rostock" title="Rostock">Rostock</a> (950&#160;km) at the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> are closer to Trieste than Odessa yet it is not considered as another European peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Since the late 19th and early 20th-century literature is not known where is exactly the northern border between the peninsula and the continent,<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> with an issue, whether the rivers are suitable for its definition.<sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In the studies the Balkans natural borders, especially the northern border, are often avoided to be addressed, considered as a "fastidious problem" by André Blanc in <i>Geography of the Balkans</i> (1965), while John Lampe and Marvin Jackman in <i>Balkan Economic History</i> (1971) noted that "modern geographers seem agreed in rejecting the old idea of a Balkan Peninsula".<sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Another issue is the name because the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Mountains" title="Balkan Mountains">Balkan Mountains</a> which are mostly located in Northern Bulgaria are not dominating the region by length and area like the <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric Alps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> An eventual Balkan peninsula can be considered a territory South of the Balkan Mountains, with a possible name "Greek-Albanian Peninsula", but Greece is rarely defined as a Balkan nation both geographically and in international relations.<sup id="cite_ref-DaskalovMishkova2017_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaskalovMishkova2017-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The term influenced the meaning of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a> which again is not properly defined by geographical factors yet historical borders of the Balkans.<sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Croatian geographers and academics are highly critical of inclusion of Croatia within the broad geographical, social-political and historical context of the Balkans, while the neologism Western Balkans is perceived as a humiliation of Croatia by the European political powers.<sup id="cite_ref-Somek15_23-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somek15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> According to M. S. Altić, the term has two different meanings, "geographical, ultimately undefined, and cultural, extremely negative, and recently strongly motivated by the contemporary political context".<sup id="cite_ref-Altić11_24-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altić11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Croatia" title="President of Croatia">President of Croatia</a> <a href="/wiki/Kolinda_Grabar-Kitarovi%C4%87" title="Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović">Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović</a> stated that the use of the term "Western Balkans" should be avoided because it doesn't imply only a geographic area, but also negative connotations, and instead must be perceived as and called Southeast Europe because it is part of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_and_natural_resources">Nature and natural resources</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Todorini_kukli_north.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Todorini_kukli_north.jpg/220px-Todorini_kukli_north.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Todorini_kukli_north.jpg/330px-Todorini_kukli_north.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Todorini_kukli_north.jpg/440px-Todorini_kukli_north.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Todorini_kukli_north.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panorama of <a href="/wiki/Stara_Planina" class="mw-redirect" title="Stara Planina">Stara Planina</a>. Its highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Botev_Peak" title="Botev Peak">Botev</a> at a height of 2,376&#160;m.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg/220px-Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg/330px-Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg/440px-Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marichin_cirkus_IMG_1452.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View toward <a href="/wiki/Rila" title="Rila">Rila</a>, the highest mountain in the Balkans which reaches 2925&#160;m</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg/220px-Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg/330px-Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg/440px-Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lac_de_Shkodra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Skadar" title="Lake Skadar">Lake Skadar</a>, the largest lake in the Balkan Peninsula</div></div></div>
<p>Most of the area is covered by mountain ranges running from the northwest to southeast. The main ranges are the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan mountains">Balkan mountains</a> (Stara Planina in <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian language</a>), running from the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coast in <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> to the border with <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rila" title="Rila">Rilo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Rhodope_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhodope mountains">Rhodope</a> <a href="/wiki/Massif" title="Massif">massif</a> in southern Bulgaria, northern <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and southeastern <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric Alps</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, the <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar</a> massif which spreads from <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> to <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pindus" title="Pindus">Pindus</a> range, spanning from southern Albania into central Greece and the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Alps" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian Alps">Albanian Alps</a>. The highest mountain of the region is <a href="/wiki/Rila" title="Rila">Rila</a> in Bulgaria, with <a href="/wiki/Musala" title="Musala">Musala</a> at 2925&#160;m, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Olympus_(Mountain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Olympus (Mountain)">Mount Olympus</a> in Greece, being second at 2917&#160;m and <a href="/wiki/Vihren" title="Vihren">Vihren</a> in Bulgaria being the third at 2914&#160;m. The <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> field or <a href="/wiki/Polje" title="Polje">polje</a> is a common feature of the landscape.
</p><p>On the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean</a> coasts the climate is <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a>, on the Black Sea coast the climate is <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a>, and inland it is <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental</a>. In the northern part of the peninsula and on the mountains, winters are frosty and snowy, while summers are hot and dry. In the southern part winters are milder. The humid continental climate is predominant in Bosnia and Herzegovina, northern Croatia, Bulgaria, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, northern Montenegro, the Republic of North Macedonia, the interior of Albania and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, while the other, less common climates, the humid subtropical and oceanic climates, are seen on the Black Sea coast of Bulgaria and <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">Balkan Turkey (European Turkey)</a>; and the Mediterranean climate is seen on the coast of Albania, the coast of Croatia, Greece, southern Montenegro and the Aegean coast of <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">Balkan Turkey (European Turkey)</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Over the centuries forests have been cut down and replaced with <a href="/wiki/Bush_(plant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bush (plant)">bush</a>. In the southern part and on the coast there is <a href="/wiki/Evergreen" title="Evergreen">evergreen</a> vegetation. Inland there are woods typical of Central Europe (<a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">beech</a>, and in the mountains, <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">spruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fir" title="Fir">fir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">tree line</a> in the mountains lies at the height of 1800–2300&#160;m. The land provides <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitats</a> for numerous <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> species, including extraordinarily abundant insects and reptiles that serve as food for a variety of <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_prey" class="mw-redirect" title="Birds of prey">birds of prey</a> and rare <a href="/wiki/Vulture" title="Vulture">vultures</a>.
</p><p>The soils are generally poor, except on the <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a>, where areas with natural grass, fertile soils and warm summers provide an opportunity for tillage. Elsewhere, land cultivation is mostly unsuccessful because of the mountains, hot summers and poor soils, although certain cultures such as <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olive</a> and grape flourish.
</p><p>Resources of energy are scarce, except in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, where considerable <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">chromium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a> deposits are located.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Other deposits of <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, especially in Bulgaria, Serbia and Bosnia, also exist. <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">Lignite</a> deposits are widespread in Greece. <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Petroleum</a> scarce reserves exist in Greece, Serbia and Albania. Natural gas deposits are scarce. <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">Hydropower</a> is in wide use, from over 1,000 dams. The often relentless <a href="/wiki/Bora_wind" class="mw-redirect" title="Bora wind">bora wind</a> is also being harnessed for power generation.
</p><p>Metal ores are more usual than other raw materials. Iron ore is rare, but in some countries there is a considerable amount of copper, zinc, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromite" title="Chromite">chromite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesite" title="Magnesite">magnesite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>. Some metals are exported.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_and_geopolitical_significance">History and geopolitical significance</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg/220px-Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg/330px-Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg/440px-Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg 2x" data-file-width="614" data-file-height="561" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bgiusca_Jirecek_Line.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Jire%C4%8Dek_Line" title="Jireček Line">Jireček Line</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Appolonia_Albania.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Appolonia_Albania.jpg/220px-Appolonia_Albania.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Appolonia_Albania.jpg/330px-Appolonia_Albania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Appolonia_Albania.jpg/440px-Appolonia_Albania.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4237" data-file-height="2825" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Appolonia_Albania.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Apollonia_(Illyria)" title="Apollonia (Illyria)">Apollonia</a> ruins near <a href="/wiki/Fier" title="Fier">Fier</a>, Albania.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_(19629095974).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_%2819629095974%29.jpg/220px-The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_%2819629095974%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_%2819629095974%29.jpg/330px-The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_%2819629095974%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_%2819629095974%29.jpg/440px-The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_%2819629095974%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4443" data-file-height="2962" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_new_old_amphitheater_in_Pula_Istria_(19629095974).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pula_Arena" title="Pula Arena">Pula Arena</a>, the only remaining Roman amphitheatre to have four side towers and with all three Roman architectural orders entirely preserved.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Balkans" title="History of the Balkans">History of the Balkans</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span></h3>
<p>The Balkan region was the first area in Europe to experience the arrival of farming cultures in the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> era. The Balkans have been inhabited since the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> and are the route by which farming from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> spread to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> (7th millennium BC).<sup id="cite_ref-Borza_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borza-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The practices of growing grain and raising livestock arrived in the Balkans from the <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a> by way of <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> and spread west and north into Central Europe, particularly through <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>. Two early culture-complexes have developed in the region, <a href="/wiki/Star%C4%8Devo_culture" title="Starčevo culture">Starčevo culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da_culture" title="Vinča culture">Vinča culture</a>. The Balkans are also the location of the first advanced civilizations. Vinča culture developed a form of <a href="/wiki/Proto-writing" title="Proto-writing">proto-writing</a> before the <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumerians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minoans" class="mw-redirect" title="Minoans">Minoans</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Old_European_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Old European script">Old European script</a>, while the bulk of the symbols had been created in the period between 4500 and 4000 BC, with the ones on the Tărtăria clay tablets even dating back to around 5300 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-GdS_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GdS-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The identity of the Balkans is dominated by its geographical position; historically the area was known as a crossroads of cultures. It has been a juncture between the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> bodies of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, the destination of a massive influx of pagan <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, an area where <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> Christianity met,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> as well as the meeting point between <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and Christianity.
</p><p>In pre-classical and <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>, this region was home to <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paeonians" class="mw-redirect" title="Paeonians">Paeonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dacians" title="Dacians">Dacians</a>, and other ancient groups. The <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Persian Empire</a> incorporated parts of the Balkans comprising <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coastal region of <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> between the late 6th and the first half of the 5th-century BC into its territories.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Later the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> conquered most of the region and spread Roman culture and the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> language, but significant parts still remained under <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">classical Greek</a> influence. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> considered the <a href="/wiki/Rhodope_Mountains" title="Rhodope Mountains">Rhodope Mountains</a> to be the northern limit of the Peninsula of Haemus and the same limit applied approximately to the border between Greek and Latin use in the region (later called the <a href="/wiki/Jire%C4%8Dek_Line" title="Jireček Line">Jireček Line</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> However large spaces south of Jireček Line were and are inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Vlachs" title="Vlachs">Vlachs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aromanians" title="Aromanians">Aromanians</a>), the Romance-speaking heirs of Roman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Slavs" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Slavs">Slavs</a> arrived in the 6th-century and began assimilating and displacing already-assimilated (through Romanization and Hellenization) older inhabitants of the northern and central Balkans, forming the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the Balkans became the stage for a series of wars between the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Roman</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian</a> Empires.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span></h3>
<p>By the end of the 16th-century, the Ottoman Empire had become the controlling force in the region after expanding from Anatolia through <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a> to the Balkans. Many people in the Balkans place their greatest folk heroes in the era of either the onslaught or the retreat of the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> As examples, for Greeks, <a href="/wiki/Constantine_XI_Palaiologos" title="Constantine XI Palaiologos">Constantine XI Palaiologos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kolokotronis" class="mw-redirect" title="Kolokotronis">Kolokotronis</a>; and for <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Obili%C4%87" title="Miloš Obilić">Miloš Obilić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lazar_Hrebeljanovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Lazar Hrebeljanović">Tzar Lazar</a>; for <a href="/wiki/Montenegrins_(ethnic_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrins (ethnic group)">Montenegrins</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%90ura%C4%91_I_Bal%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Đurađ I Balšić">Đurađ I Balšić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Crnojevi%C4%87" title="Ivan Crnojević">Ivan Crnojević</a>; for <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Kastrioti_Skanderbeg" class="mw-redirect" title="George Kastrioti Skanderbeg">George Kastrioti Skanderbeg</a>; for <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Macedonians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Macedonians">ethnic Macedonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Karev" title="Nikola Karev">Nikola Karev</a><sup id="cite_ref-Considered_a_Bulgarian_in_Bulgaria_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Considered_a_Bulgarian_in_Bulgaria-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Goce_Del%C4%8Dev" class="mw-redirect" title="Goce Delčev">Goce Delčev</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Considered_a_Bulgarian_in_Bulgaria_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Considered_a_Bulgarian_in_Bulgaria-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasil_Levski" title="Vasil Levski">Vasil Levski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Sava_Rakovski" title="Georgi Sava Rakovski">Georgi Sava Rakovski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hristo_Botev" title="Hristo Botev">Hristo Botev</a> and for <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_%C5%A0ubi%C4%87_Zrinjski" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikola Šubić Zrinjski">Nikola Šubić Zrinjski</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif/220px-Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif/330px-Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif/440px-Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="618" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkans_Animation_1800-2008.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Modern political history of the Balkans from 1796 onwards.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG/220px-Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG/330px-Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG/440px-Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_81.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox Christian">Eastern Orthodox Christian</a> cathedral built in the 6th-century in <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> (present-day Istanbul, Turkey), later an imperial mosque, and now a museum.</div></div></div>
<p>In the past several centuries, because of the frequent <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">Ottoman wars in Europe</a> fought in and around the Balkans and the comparative Ottoman isolation from the mainstream of economic advance (reflecting the shift of Europe's commercial and political centre of gravity towards the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a>), the Balkans has been the least developed part of Europe. According to <a href="/wiki/Halil_%C4%B0nalc%C4%B1k" title="Halil İnalcık">Halil İnalcık</a>, "The population of the Balkans, according to one estimate, <a href="/wiki/Population_decline" title="Population decline">fell from a high of 8 million</a> in the late 16th-century to only 3 million by the mid-eighteenth. This estimate is based on Ottoman documentary evidence."<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most of the Balkan nation-states emerged during the 19th and early 20th centuries as they gained independence from the Ottoman Empire or the Austro-Hungarian empire: Greece in 1821, Serbia, Montenegro in 1878, Romania in 1881, Bulgaria in 1908 and Albania in 1912.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tsarevets.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Tsarevets.JPG/220px-Tsarevets.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Tsarevets.JPG/330px-Tsarevets.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Tsarevets.JPG/440px-Tsarevets.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tsarevets.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tsarevets_(fortress)" title="Tsarevets (fortress)">Tsarevets</a>, a medieval stronghold in the former capital of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian Empire</a> — <a href="/wiki/Veliko_Tarnovo" title="Veliko Tarnovo">Veliko Tarnovo</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohrid_Lake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Ohrid_Lake.jpg/220px-Ohrid_Lake.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Ohrid_Lake.jpg/330px-Ohrid_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Ohrid_Lake.jpg/440px-Ohrid_Lake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohrid_Lake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 13th-century <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._John_at_Kaneo" title="Church of St. John at Kaneo">church of St. John at Kaneo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ohrid_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohrid Lake">Ohrid Lake</a> in North Macedonia. The lake and town were declared a <a href="/wiki/Table_of_World_Heritage_Sites_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Table of World Heritage Sites by country">World Heritage Site</a> by UNESCO in 1980.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wars">World Wars</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG/220px-Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG/330px-Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG/440px-Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2601" data-file-height="1829" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Austro-Hungarian troops executing Serbian civilians, 1914. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Serbia</a> lost about 850,000 people during the war, a quarter of its pre-war population.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In 1912–1913 the <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a> broke out when the nation-states of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria" title="Kingdom of Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Greece_(Gl%C3%BCcksburg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Greece (Glücksburg)">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Montenegro</a> united in an <a href="/wiki/Balkan_League" title="Balkan League">alliance</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. As a result of the war, almost all remaining European territories of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> were captured and partitioned among the allies. Ensuing events also led to the creation of an independent <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albanian</a> state. Bulgaria insisted on its status quo territorial integrity, divided and shared by the Great Powers next to the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–78)">Russo-Turkish War (1877–78)</a> in other boundaries and on the pre-war Bulgarian-Serbian agreement. Bulgaria was provoked by the backstage deals between its former allies, Serbia and Greece, on the allocation of the spoils at the end of the First Balkan War. At the time, Bulgaria was fighting at the main Thracian Front. Bulgaria marks the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Second_Balkan_War" title="Second Balkan War">Second Balkan War</a> when it attacked them. The Serbs and the Greeks repulsed single attacks, but when the Greek army invaded Bulgaria together with an unprovoked Romanian intervention in the back, Bulgaria collapsed. The Ottoman Empire used the opportunity to recapture <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Thrace" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Thrace">Eastern Thrace</a>, establishing its new western borders that still stand today as part of modern Turkey.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> was sparked in the Balkans in 1914 when members of <a href="/wiki/Young_Bosnia" title="Young Bosnia">Young Bosnia</a>, a revolutionary organization with predominantly Serb and pro-Yugoslav members, <a href="/wiki/Assassination_in_Sarajevo" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination in Sarajevo">assassinated</a> the Austro-Hungarian heir <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria">Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria</a> in Bosnia and Herzegovina's capital, <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>. That caused a war between Austria-Hungary and Serbia, which—through the existing <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">chains of alliances</a>—led to the First World War. The Ottoman Empire soon joined the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> becoming one of the three empires participating in that alliance. The next year Bulgaria joined the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> attacking Serbia, which was successfully fighting Austro-Hungary to the north for a year. That led to Serbia's defeat and the intervention of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Entente</a> in the Balkans which sent an expeditionary force to establish a new <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_front" title="Macedonian front">front</a>, the third one of that war, which soon also became static. The participation of Greece in the war three years later, in 1918, on the part of the Entente finally altered the balance between the opponents leading to the collapse of the common German-Bulgarian front there, which caused the exit of Bulgaria from the war, and in turn the collapse of the Austro-Hungarian Empire, ending the First World War.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the start of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, all Balkan countries, with the exception of Greece, were allies of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, having bilateral military agreements or being part of the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Pact" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Pact">Axis Pact</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Fascist Italy</a> expanded the war in the Balkans by using its protectorate Albania to <a href="/wiki/Greco-Italian_War" title="Greco-Italian War">invade Greece</a>. After repelling the attack, the Greeks counterattacked, invading Italy-held Albania and causing Nazi Germany's intervention in the Balkans to help its ally.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Days before the German invasion, a successful <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;état">coup d'état</a> in Belgrade by neutral military personnel seized power.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the new government reaffirmed Serbia's intentions to fulfill its obligations as a member of the Axis,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchreiber,_Stegemann_and_Vogel1995484_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchreiber,_Stegemann_and_Vogel1995484-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Germany, with Bulgaria, invaded both Greece and Yugoslavia. Yugoslavia immediately disintegrated when those loyal to the Serbian King and the Croatian units mutinied.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchreiber,_Stegemann_and_Vogel1995521_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchreiber,_Stegemann_and_Vogel1995521-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Greece resisted, but, after two months of fighting, collapsed and was occupied. The two countries were partitioned between the three Axis allies, Bulgaria, Germany and Italy, and the <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Independent State of Croatia</a>, a puppet state of Italy and Germany.
</p><p>During the occupation the population suffered considerable hardship due to repression and starvation, to which the population reacted by creating a mass resistance movement.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Together with the early and extremely heavy winter of that year (which caused hundreds of thousands deaths among the poorly fed population), the German invasion had disastrous effects in the timetable of the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">planned invasion in Russia</a> causing a significant delay,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> which had major consequences during the course of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Finally, at the end of 1944, the Soviets entered Romania and Bulgaria forcing the Germans out of the Balkans. They left behind a region largely ruined as a result of wartime exploitation.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War">Cold War</span></h4>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, most of the countries on the Balkans were governed by communist governments. Greece became the first battleground of the emerging Cold War. The <a href="/wiki/Truman_Doctrine" title="Truman Doctrine">Truman Doctrine</a> was the US response to the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Civil_War" title="Greek Civil War">civil war</a>, which raged from 1944 to 1949. This civil war, unleashed by the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Greece" title="Communist Party of Greece">Communist Party of Greece</a>, backed by communist volunteers from neighboring countries (Albania, Bulgaria and Yugoslavia), led to massive American assistance for the non-communist Greek government. With this backing, Greece managed to defeat the partisans and, ultimately, remained the only non-communist country in the region.
</p><p>However, despite being under communist governments, <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> (1948) and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania" title="People&#39;s Socialist Republic of Albania">Albania</a> (1961) fell out with the Soviet Union. Yugoslavia, led by Marshal <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a> (1892–1980), first propped up then rejected the idea of merging with <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and instead sought closer relations with the West, later even spearheaded, together with India and Egypt the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. Albania on the other hand gravitated toward <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">Communist China</a>, later adopting an <a href="/wiki/Isolationism" title="Isolationism">isolationist</a> position.
</p><p>As the only non-communist countries, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> were (and still are) part of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> composing the southeastern wing of the alliance.
</p>
<h4><span id="Post.E2.80.93Cold_War"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post–Cold_War">Post–Cold War</span></h4>
<p>In the 1990s, the transition of the regions' ex-Eastern bloc countries towards democratic free-market societies went peacefully. While in the non-alligned <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Wars between the former Yugoslav republics</a> broke out after Slovenia and Croatia held free elections and their people voted for independence on their respective countries' referenda. Serbia in turn declared the dissolution of the union as unconstitutional and the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_People%27s_Army" title="Yugoslav People&#39;s Army">Yugoslavian army</a> unsuccessfully tried to maintain status quo. Slovenia and Croatia declared independence on 25 June 1991, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Ten-Day_War" title="Ten-Day War">Ten-Day War</a> in Slovenia. Till October 1991, the Army withdrew from Slovenia, and in Croatia, the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_War_of_Independence" title="Croatian War of Independence">Croatian War of Independence</a> would continue <a href="/wiki/Operation_Storm" title="Operation Storm">until 1995</a>. In the ensuing 10 years armed confrontation, gradually all the other Republics declared independence, with <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnia being the most affected</a> by the fighting. The long lasting wars resulted in a United Nations intervention and <a href="/wiki/NATO_intervention_in_Bosnia" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO intervention in Bosnia">NATO</a> ground and air forces <a href="/wiki/1995_NATO_bombing_campaign_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="1995 NATO bombing campaign in Bosnia and Herzegovina">took action against Serb forces</a> in Bosnia and Herzegovina and <a href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">Serbia</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG/250px-Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG" decoding="async" width="250" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG/375px-Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG/500px-Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1887" data-file-height="1242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_Yugoslavia_2008.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>State entities on the former territory of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, 2008</div></div></div>
<p>From the dissolution of Yugoslavia six republics achieved international recognition as sovereign republics, but these are traditionally included in Balkans: <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. In 2008, while under UN administration, Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">declared independence</a> (according to the official Serbian policy, Kosovo is still an internal autonomous region). In July 2010, the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>, ruled that the declaration of independence was legal.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Most UN member states recognise Kosovo. After the end of the wars a <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Overthrow of Slobodan Milošević">revolution</a> broke in Serbia and <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a>, the Serbian communist leader (elected president between 1989 and 2000), was overthrown and handed for trial to the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal</a> for crimes against the <a href="/wiki/International_Humanitarian_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="International Humanitarian Law">International Humanitarian Law</a> during the Yugoslav wars. Milošević died of a heart attack in 2006 before a verdict could have been released. Ιn 2001 an <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Insurgency in the Republic of Macedonia">Albanian uprising</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> forced the country to give local autonomy to the <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in Macedonia">ethnic Albanians</a> in the areas where they predominate.
</p><p>With the dissolution of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> an issue emerged over the name under which the former (federated) republic of Macedonia would internationally be recognized, between the new country and Greece. Being the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonian part of Yugoslavia</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Vardar_Macedonia" title="Vardar Macedonia">Vardar Macedonia</a>), the federated Republic under the Yugoslav identity had the name <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Socialist Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a> on which it declared its sovereignty in 1991. Greece, having a large region (see <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(Greece)" title="Macedonia (Greece)">Macedonia</a>) also under the same name opposed to the usage of this name as an indication of a nationality. The <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">issue</a> was resolved under UN mediation and the <a href="/wiki/Prespa_agreement" title="Prespa agreement">Prespa agreement</a> was reached, which saw the country's renaming into North Macedonia.
</p><p>Balkan countries control the direct <a href="/wiki/European_route" class="mw-redirect" title="European route">land routes</a> between Western Europe and South West Asia (<a href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia Minor">Asia Minor</a> and the Middle East). Since 2000, all Balkan countries are friendly towards the EU and the USA.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> since 1981 while <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> is a member since 2004, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> are members since 2007, and <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> is a member since 2013. In 2005, the European Union decided to start accession negotiations with candidate countries; <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> were accepted as candidates for EU membership. In 2012, Montenegro started <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Montenegro_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Montenegro to the European Union">accession negotiations</a> with the EU. In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Albania_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Albania to the European Union">official candidate</a> for accession to the EU. In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> was expected to start <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">accession negotiations</a> with the EU, however this process has been stalled over the recognition of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> as an independent state by existing EU member states.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> have been <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> members since 1952. In March 2004, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> have become members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. As of April 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> are members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> joined in June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All other countries have expressed a desire to join the EU or NATO at some point in the future.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_economy">Politics and economy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oia,_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Oia%2C_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg/220px-Oia%2C_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Oia%2C_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg/330px-Oia%2C_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Oia%2C_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg/440px-Oia%2C_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1776" data-file-height="1178" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oia,_Santorini_HDR_sunset.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View from <a href="/wiki/Santorini" title="Santorini">Santorini</a> in Greece. <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Greece" title="Tourism in Greece">Tourism</a> is an important part of the Greek economy.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG/220px-Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG/330px-Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG/440px-Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dubrovnik_june_2011..JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a> in Croatia, UNESCO's <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage">World Heritage</a> since 1979</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sveti_Stefan_(06).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Sveti_Stefan_%2806%29.jpg/220px-Sveti_Stefan_%2806%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Sveti_Stefan_%2806%29.jpg/330px-Sveti_Stefan_%2806%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Sveti_Stefan_%2806%29.jpg/440px-Sveti_Stefan_%2806%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4674" data-file-height="2629" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sveti_Stefan_(06).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sveti_Stefan" title="Sveti Stefan">Sveti Stefan</a>, popular tourist destination and an island-hotel on <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegrin coast</a></div></div></div>
<p>Currently all of the states are republics, but until World War II all countries were monarchies. Most of the republics are <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary</a>, excluding Romania and Bosnia which are <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a>. All the states have <a href="/wiki/Open_economy" title="Open economy">open</a> <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economies</a>, most of which are in the upper-middle income range ($4,000 – $12,000 p.c.), except <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> that have <a href="/wiki/High_income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High income economy">high income economies</a> (over $12,000 p.c.), and are classified with very high <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">HDI</a>, along with Bulgaria, in contrast to the remaining states, which are classified with high HDI. The states from the former <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> that formerly had <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a> system and Turkey mark gradual economic growth each year, only the economy of Greece drops for 2012 and meanwhile it was expected to grow in 2013. The Gross domestic product (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">Purchasing power parity</a>) per capita is highest in Slovenia (over $36,000), followed by Greece (over $30,000), Croatia, Bulgaria and Romania (over $23,000), Turkey, Montenegro, Serbia, North Macedonia ($10,000 – $15,000) and Bosnia, Albania and Kosovo (below $10,000).<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a>, which indicates the level of difference by monetary welfare of the layers, is on the second level at the highest monetary equality in Albania, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and Serbia, on the third level in Greece, Montenegro and Romania, on the fourth level in North Macedonia, on the fifth level in Turkey, and the most unequal by Gini coefficient is Bosnia at the eighth level which is the penultimate level and one of the highest in the world. The unemployment is lowest in Romania and Bulgaria (below 6%), followed by Turkey, Albania (10 – 15%), Greece (15 – 20%), Montenegro, Serbia, Bosnia (20 – 30%), North Macedonia (over 30%) and Kosovo (over 40%).
</p>
<ul><li>On political, social and economic criteria the divisions are as follows:
<ul><li>Territories <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">members</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>: Bulgaria, Croatia, Greece, Romania and Slovenia</li>
<li>Territories currently in <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union#Current_agenda" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">negotiation process</a> for EU membership: Montenegro, Serbia and Turkey</li>
<li>Territories <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union#Current_agenda" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">official candidates</a> for EU membership: Albania and North Macedonia</li>
<li>Territories with "<a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union#Current_agenda" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">potential candidates</a>" status for EU membership: Bosnia and Herzegovina and Kosovo</li></ul></li>
<li>On border control and trade criteria the divisions are as follows:
<ul><li>Territories in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>: Greece and Slovenia</li>
<li>Territories that are legally bound to join the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>: Bulgaria, Croatia and Romania</li>
<li>Territories in a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">customs union</a> with the EU: Turkey</li>
<li>Territories members of the <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central European Free Trade Agreement">Central European Free Trade Agreement</a>: Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Kosovo, Montenegro, North Macedonia and Serbia.</li></ul></li>
<li>On currency criteria the divisions are as follows:
<ul><li>Territories members of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>: Greece and Slovenia</li>
<li>Territories using the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> without authorization by the EU: Kosovo and Montenegro</li>
<li>Territories using national currencies and are <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_eurozone" title="Enlargement of the eurozone">candidates</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>: Bulgaria (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_lev" title="Bulgarian lev">lev</a>), Croatia (<a href="/wiki/Croatian_kuna" title="Croatian kuna">kuna</a>), Romania (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_leu" title="Romanian leu">leu</a>)</li>
<li>Territories using national currencies: Albania (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_lek" title="Albanian lek">lek</a>), Bosnia and Herzegovina (<a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_convertible_mark" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina convertible mark">convertible mark</a>), North Macedonia (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_denar" title="Macedonian denar">denar</a>), Serbia (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_dinar" title="Serbian dinar">dinar</a>) and Turkey (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">lira</a>).</li></ul></li>
<li>On military criteria the divisions are as follows:<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg/220px-Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg/330px-Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg/440px-Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial photo of <a href="/wiki/Camp_Bondsteel" title="Camp Bondsteel">Camp Bondsteel</a>, the main base of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> under <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a> command in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO" title="Member states of NATO">Member territories</a> of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>: Albania, Bulgaria, Croatia, Greece, Montenegro, Romania, Slovenia and Turkey</li>
<li>Member territories of the <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> with <a href="/wiki/Individual_Partnership_Action_Plan" title="Individual Partnership Action Plan">Individual Partnership Action Plan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Membership_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Membership Action Plan">Membership Action Plan</a> for joining NATO: Bosnia and Herzegovina and North Macedonia</li>
<li>Member territories of the <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a>: Serbia</li></ul></li>
<li>On the recent political, social and economic criteria there are two groups of countries:
<ul><li>Former communist territories: Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Bulgaria, Croatia, Kosovo, Montenegro, North Macedonia, Romania, Serbia and Slovenia</li>
<li>Territories with capitalist past: Greece and Turkey</li>
<li>During the Cold War the Balkans were disputed between the two blocks. Greece and Turkey were members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, Bulgaria and Romania of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>, while Yugoslavia was proponent of a third way and was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. After the dissolution of Yugoslavia, Serbia and Bosnia and Herzegovina kept an observer status within the organisation.</li></ul></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<p>The region is inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aromanians" title="Aromanians">Aromanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gorani_people" title="Gorani people">Gorani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_(ethnic_group)" title="Macedonians (ethnic group)">Macedonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegrins" title="Montenegrins">Montenegrins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenes" title="Slovenes">Slovenes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, and other ethnic groups which present minorities in certain countries like the <a href="/wiki/Romani_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Romani People">Romani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashkali" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashkali">Ashkali</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (May 2016)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AtlBalkrelig.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/AtlBalkrelig.jpg/250px-AtlBalkrelig.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/90/AtlBalkrelig.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="318" data-file-height="327" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AtlBalkrelig.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing religious denominations</div></div></div>
<p>The region is a meeting point of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-okey_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-okey-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Eastern Orthodoxy is the majority religion in both the Balkan peninsula and the Balkan region. A variety of different traditions of each faith are practiced, with each of the Eastern Orthodox countries having its own national church. A part of the population in the Balkans defines itself as irreligious.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG/220px-Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="320" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG/330px-Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG/440px-Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Albania_confessional_map_with_regions_circa_1900.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Approximate distribution of religions in <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a></div></div></div>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> communities of the Balkans were some of the oldest in Europe and date back to ancient times. These communities were <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a>, except in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, where the Jewish communities were mainly <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, the small and close-knit Jewish community is 90% <a href="/wiki/Sephardic" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic">Sephardic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judeo-Spanish" class="mw-redirect" title="Judeo-Spanish">Ladino</a> is still spoken among the elderly. The Sephardi Jewish cemetery in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> has tombstones of a unique shape and inscribed in ancient Ladino.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Sephardi Jews used to have a large presence in the city of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, and by 1900, some 80,000, or more than half of the population, were Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The Jewish communities in the Balkans suffered immensely during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, and the vast majority were killed during the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a>. An exception were the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Jews">Bulgarian Jews</a>, most of whom were saved by <a href="/wiki/Boris_III_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris III of Bulgaria">Boris III of Bulgaria</a>, who resisted <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>, opposing their deportation to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>. Almost all of the few survivors have emigrated to the (then) newly founded state of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and elsewhere. Almost no Balkan country today has a significant Jewish minority.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg/200px-Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg/300px-Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg/400px-Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg 2x" data-file-width="716" data-file-height="563" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ernst-Ravenstein-Balkans-Ethnic-Map-1880.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ethnic map of the Balkans (1880)</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Balkans" title="Languages of the Balkans">Languages of the Balkans</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Balkan_sprachbund" title="Balkan sprachbund">Balkan sprachbund</a></div>
<p>The Balkan region today is a very diverse ethno-linguistic region, being home to multiple <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkish</a>, and others. <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> is spoken by a large portion of the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romanis</a> living throughout the Balkan countries. Throughout history many other ethnic groups with their own languages lived in the area, among them <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> and various <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a>. All of the aforementioned languages from the present and from the past belong to the wider <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> language family, with the exception of the Turkic languages (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gagauz_language" title="Gagauz language">Gagauz</a>).
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="font-size: 90%;">

<tbody><tr>
<th>State</th>
<th>Most spoken language<sup id="cite_ref-languages_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-languages-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</th>
<th>Linguistic minorities<sup id="cite_ref-languages_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-languages-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
