<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span></h3>
<p>Most of the states in the Balkans are predominantly urbanized, with the lowest number of urban population as&#160;% of the total population found in Kosovo at under 40%, Bosnia and Herzegovina at 40% and Slovenia at 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:758px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg" class="image" title="Panoramic view of Istanbul"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg/750px-Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg" decoding="async" width="750" height="162" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg/1125px-Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg/1500px-Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="1123" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg" title="File:Istanbul panorama and skyline.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of Istanbul</div></div></div>

<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_reference_name_Aa"><a href="#ref_reference_name_Aa"><b><sup>a</sup></b></a></span>  Only the European part of Istanbul is a part of the Balkans.<sup id="cite_ref-Crampton_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crampton-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> It is home to two thirds of the city's 15,987,888 inhabitants.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Time_zones">Time zones</span></h2>
<p>The time zones in the Balkans are defined as the following:
</p>
<ul><li>Territories in the time zone of <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B01:00" title="UTC+01:00">UTC+01:00</a>: Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Croatia, Kosovo, Montenegro, North Macedonia, Serbia and Slovenia</li>
<li>Territories in the time zone of <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B02:00" title="UTC+02:00">UTC+02:00</a>: Bulgaria, Greece, Romania and Turkey</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
</div>
<table style="margin-left:13px; line-height:150%">
<tbody><tr>
<td align="right" valign="top">a.&#160;&#160;
</td>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_status"><b><a href="#ref_status">^</a></b></span> Kosovo is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008, but <a href="/wiki/Kosovo%E2%80%93Serbia_relations" title="Kosovo–Serbia relations">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">2013 Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo has been recognized as an independent state by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">112</a> out of 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations member states</a>, while <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">12</a> states have recognized Kosovo only to later withdraw their recognition.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<table style="margin-left:13px; line-height:150%">
<tbody><tr>
<td align="right" valign="top">b.&#160;&#160;
</td>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_location"><b><a href="#ref_location">^</a></b></span>  As <i>The World Factbook</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/geos/tu.html">cites</a>, regarding Turkey and Southeastern Europe; "that portion of Turkey west of the Bosphorus is geographically part of Europe."
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
</div>
<table style="margin-left:13px; line-height:150%">

</td>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_European_Turkey"><b><a href="#ref_European_Turkey">^</a></b></span> The population only of <a href="/wiki/European_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="European Turkey">European Turkey</a>, that excludes the <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatolian peninsula">Anatolian peninsula</a>, which otherwise has a population of 75,627,384 and a density of 97.

Pavlowitch, <i>A History of the Balkans 1804-1945</i> (Routledge, 2014).</span>

<li id="cite_note-EB-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-EB_43-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EB_43-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EB_43-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/50325/Balkans">"Balkans"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">21 August</span> 2019</span>. <q>The Balkans are usually characterized as comprising Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Bulgaria, Croatia, Kosovo, Montenegro, North Macedonia, Romania, Serbia, and Slovenia—with all or part of each of those countries located within the peninsula. Portions of Greece and Turkey are also located within the geographic region generally defined as the Balkan Peninsula, and many descriptions of the Balkans include those countries too. Some define the region in cultural and historical terms and others geographically, though there are even different interpretations among historians and geographers....Generally, the Balkans are bordered on the northwest by Italy, on the north by Hungary, on the north and northeast by Moldova and Ukraine, and on the south by Greece and Turkey or the Aegean Sea (depending on how the region is defined)...For discussion of physical and human geography, along with the history of individual countries in the region, see Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Bulgaria, Croatia, Greece, Kosovo, North Macedonia, Moldova, Montenegro, Romania, Serbia, Slovenia, and Turkey. Area 257,400 square miles (666,700 square km). Pop. (2002 est.) 59,297,000.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Balkans&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.britannica.com%2FEBchecked%2Ftopic%2F50325%2FBalkans&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABalkans" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to an earlier version of the <i>Britannica</i>, cited in Crampton, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=z9AFBAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PT14">The Balkans Since the Second World War</a>, the Balkans comprise "the territory of the states of Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Bulgaria, Croatia, Greece, Macedonia, Moldova, Romania, Slovenia and Yugoslavia (Montenegro and Serbia)", and also "the European portion of Turkey"; noting that Turkey is not a Balkan state and that the inclusion of Slovenia and the <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvanian</a> part of Romania in the region is dubious.</span>
</li>
